<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yorkshire_and_the_Humber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport_policy">Transport policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yorkshire_and_the_Humber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Transport policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ouse_Motorway_Bridge.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Ouse_Motorway_Bridge.jpg/220px-Ouse_Motorway_Bridge.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Ouse_Motorway_Bridge.jpg/330px-Ouse_Motorway_Bridge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Ouse_Motorway_Bridge.jpg/440px-Ouse_Motorway_Bridge.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ouse_Motorway_Bridge.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>M62 <a href="/wiki/Ouse_Bridge_(M62)" title="Ouse Bridge (M62)">Ouse Bridge</a>, built in 1976</div></div></div>
<p>As part of the national transport planning system, the <a href="/wiki/Regional_Assemblies_in_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Regional Assemblies in England">Regional Assembly</a> is required to produce a Regional Transport Strategy to provide long-term planning for transport in the region. This involves region wide transport schemes such as those carried out by the <a href="/wiki/Highways_Agency" class="mw-redirect" title="Highways Agency">Highways Agency</a> and <a href="/wiki/Network_Rail" title="Network Rail">Network Rail</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GoYH1_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GoYH1-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
Within the region the local transport authorities plan for the future by producing <a href="/wiki/Local_transport_plan" title="Local transport plan">Local Transport Plans (LTP)</a> which outline their strategies, policies and implementation programmes.<sup id="cite_ref-DfT1_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DfT1-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The most recent LTP is that for the period 2006–11. In the Yorkshire and The Humber region the following transport authorities have published their LTP online: <a href="/wiki/East_Riding_of_Yorkshire" title="East Riding of Yorkshire">East Riding of Yorkshire</a> U.A.,<sup id="cite_ref-ERYLTP_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ERYLTP-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kingston_upon_Hull" title="Kingston upon Hull">Kingston upon Hull</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-HLTP_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HLTP-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/North_East_Lincolnshire" title="North East Lincolnshire">North East Lincolnshire</a> U.A.,<sup id="cite_ref-NELLTP_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NELLTP-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/North_Lincolnshire" title="North Lincolnshire">North Lincolnshire</a> U.A.,<sup id="cite_ref-NLLTP_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NLLTP-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/North_Yorkshire" title="North Yorkshire">North Yorkshire</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-NYLTP_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYLTP-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/South_Yorkshire" title="South Yorkshire">South Yorkshire</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-SYLTP_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SYLTP-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire" title="West Yorkshire">West Yorkshire</a><sup id="cite_ref-WYLTP_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WYLTP-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/York" title="York">York</a> U.A.<sup id="cite_ref-YLTP_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-YLTP-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yorkshire_and_the_Humber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_the_M62_motorway_-_section.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Map_of_the_M62_motorway_-_section.svg/220px-Map_of_the_M62_motorway_-_section.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="83" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Map_of_the_M62_motorway_-_section.svg/330px-Map_of_the_M62_motorway_-_section.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Map_of_the_M62_motorway_-_section.svg/440px-Map_of_the_M62_motorway_-_section.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="443" data-file-height="168" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_the_M62_motorway_-_section.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The M62's route in relation to the four major cities it serves: Liverpool, Manchester, Leeds and Hull.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/M62_motorway" title="M62 motorway">M62 motorway</a> is Yorkshire's main east-west thoroughfare, and north-south routes are the <a href="/wiki/M1_motorway" title="M1 motorway">M1</a> and the <a href="/wiki/A1_road_(Great_Britain)" title="A1 road (Great Britain)">A1</a>, with only the A1 continuing further north, with an upgrade to motorway status currently being built between <a href="/wiki/Leeming,_North_Yorkshire" title="Leeming, North Yorkshire">Leeming</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barton,_North_Yorkshire" title="Barton, North Yorkshire">Barton</a>. The other main north-south road in the region is the <a href="/wiki/A19_road" title="A19 road">A19</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-patlas_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-patlas-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/M180_motorway" title="M180 motorway">M180</a> (continuing as the A180) connects the ports at Grimsby and Immingham via the <a href="/wiki/M18_motorway_(Great_Britain)" title="M18 motorway (Great Britain)">M18</a> (<a href="/wiki/European_route_E22" title="European route E22">European route E22</a>).
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/A64_road" title="A64 road">A64</a> road connects areas in the North East of the region to the main body of motorways. The M1 was originally designed to finish at the A1 at Doncaster; this section became the M18 in December 1967. The section from the <a href="/wiki/Thurcroft_Interchange" title="Thurcroft Interchange">Thurcroft Interchange</a> to Leeds (originally known as the Leeds-Sheffield Spur) was essentially designed to replace the <a href="/wiki/A61_road" title="A61 road">A61</a>, which is still the main road that connects the centres of Sheffield, Barnsley, Wakefield and Leeds, and continues through Harrogate and Ripon to Thirsk. The M180 is shadowed by the <a href="/wiki/A18_road_(England)" title="A18 road (England)">A18</a>, which is the main road through Scunthorpe. The single-carriageway <a href="/wiki/A1079_road" title="A1079 road">A1079</a> connects Hull to York, and has been exceeding its designed capacity for many years.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chainbar_Rroundabout.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Chainbar_Rroundabout.jpg/220px-Chainbar_Rroundabout.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Chainbar_Rroundabout.jpg/330px-Chainbar_Rroundabout.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Chainbar_Rroundabout.jpg/440px-Chainbar_Rroundabout.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chainbar_Rroundabout.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Chain_Bar_junction" class="mw-redirect" title="Chain Bar junction">Chain Bar Interchange</a> on the M62, looking west, at the end of the M606, north of Cleckheaton</div></div></div>
<p>The main north-south and east-west routes interchange at a series of junctions to the south and east of Leeds, near Castleford. Leeds and Bradford have inner-city urban motorways, while Sheffield has the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Parkway" title="Sheffield Parkway">Sheffield Parkway</a> and Hull has the <i>Clive Sullivan Way</i> (<a href="/wiki/A63_road" title="A63 road">A63</a>) which connect the city centres with the motorway network.  Leeds has an inner-ring road network made mostly out of purpose-built motorway stretches which is mostly sub-terrain to the north of the city centre. Bradford, Huddersfield, Sheffield and York have inner-ring roads made by re-aligning existing roads while Halifax has a town-centre relief scheme made up of the Aachen Way and the North Bridge flyovers. The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Office_of_the_Traffic_Commissioner&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Office of the Traffic Commissioner (page does not exist)">Office of the Traffic Commissioner</a> central office is on the B6159 in east Leeds (Hillcrest House), which processes England and Wales <a href="/wiki/Commercial_driver%27s_license" title="Commercial driver&#39;s license">LGV and PSV licences</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Humber_Bridge" title="Humber Bridge">Humber Bridge</a>, the tallest bridge in the UK at 538&#160;feet, was the world's longest suspension bridge from 17 July 1981 until 5 April 1998; it was built to connect with a proposed new town near the <a href="/wiki/A15_road_(England)" title="A15 road (England)">A15</a>/M180 interchange.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yorkshire_and_the_Humber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Overview_of_Leeds_City_railway_station_04.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Overview_of_Leeds_City_railway_station_04.jpg/220px-Overview_of_Leeds_City_railway_station_04.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Overview_of_Leeds_City_railway_station_04.jpg/330px-Overview_of_Leeds_City_railway_station_04.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Overview_of_Leeds_City_railway_station_04.jpg/440px-Overview_of_Leeds_City_railway_station_04.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Overview_of_Leeds_City_railway_station_04.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Leeds_railway_station" title="Leeds railway station">Leeds railway station</a> is the busiest in the region.</div></div></div>
<p>The central hubs of the rail network in the region are <a href="/wiki/Leeds_railway_station" title="Leeds railway station">Leeds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield railway station">Sheffield</a> and <a href="/wiki/York_railway_station" title="York railway station">York</a>. The <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_Main_Line" title="East Coast Main Line">East Coast Main Line</a> passes through Leeds and York, operated by <a href="/wiki/London_North_Eastern_Railway" title="London North Eastern Railway">London North Eastern Railway</a> which has its headquarters in York.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Midland_Main_Line" title="Midland Main Line">Midland Main Line</a> finishes at Sheffield, with a less regular service to Leeds, operated by <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Railway" title="East Midlands Railway">East Midlands Railway</a>. East-west routes are operated by <a href="/wiki/TransPennine_Express" title="TransPennine Express">TransPennine Express</a> to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Piccadilly_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Piccadilly railway station">Manchester</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station" title="Liverpool Lime Street railway station">Liverpool</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> Leeds has a fairly extensive commuter network and an electrified section in the North of Bradford provides many commuter services. Sheffield has a smaller commuter rail network and there are also less extensive systems in Doncaster, Huddersfield, Wakefield and Harrogate, which connect the districts of the settlements to the centre by rail. The express service between Leeds and Huddersfield is notably quick.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/South_Yorkshire_Passenger_Transport_Executive" title="South Yorkshire Passenger Transport Executive">South Yorkshire Passenger Transport Executive</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire_Metro" title="West Yorkshire Metro">West Yorkshire Metro</a> subsidise commuters' travel with discount schemes. <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_399" title="British Rail Class 399">Class 399</a> <a href="/wiki/Tram-train" title="Tram-train">tram-trains</a> are to be introduced in Sheffield in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Hull is connected to <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> by <a href="/wiki/Hull_Trains" title="Hull Trains">Hull Trains</a>' services. North Yorkshire has a skeleton train network, with Scarborough and York being the main destinations. The <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Coast_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Yorkshire Coast Line">Yorkshire Coast Line</a> connects <a href="/wiki/Hull_Paragon_Interchange" title="Hull Paragon Interchange">Hull</a> to <a href="/wiki/Scarborough_railway_station" title="Scarborough railway station">Scarborough</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Hull_to_York_Line" title="Hull to York Line">Hull to York Line</a> runs along the north of the Humber through <a href="/wiki/Selby_railway_station" title="Selby railway station">Selby</a>, and takes in <a href="/wiki/Sherburn-in-Elmet_railway_station" title="Sherburn-in-Elmet railway station">Sherburn-in-Elmet</a> and nearby rural stations south of York, being of great use to commuters to York since being reopened in the 1980s.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A_HST_heads_North_to_York_-_geograph.org.uk_-_330481.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/A_HST_heads_North_to_York_-_geograph.org.uk_-_330481.jpg/140px-A_HST_heads_North_to_York_-_geograph.org.uk_-_330481.jpg" decoding="async" width="140" height="93" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/A_HST_heads_North_to_York_-_geograph.org.uk_-_330481.jpg/210px-A_HST_heads_North_to_York_-_geograph.org.uk_-_330481.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/A_HST_heads_North_to_York_-_geograph.org.uk_-_330481.jpg/280px-A_HST_heads_North_to_York_-_geograph.org.uk_-_330481.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="426" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A_HST_heads_North_to_York_-_geograph.org.uk_-_330481.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Great_North_Eastern_Railway" title="Great North Eastern Railway">GNER</a> <a href="/wiki/InterCity_125" title="InterCity 125">InterCity 125</a> near York. The InterCity 125 set the current <a href="/wiki/Land_speed_record_for_rail_vehicles" class="mw-redirect" title="Land speed record for rail vehicles">world speed record</a> for a diesel train (148&#160;mph) near Thirsk in 1987.</div></div></div>
<p>South of the Humber, <a href="/wiki/Scunthorpe_railway_station" title="Scunthorpe railway station">Scunthorpe</a> and nearby rural stations are connected by the <a href="/wiki/South_Humberside_Main_Line" title="South Humberside Main Line">South Humberside Main Line</a>, run by <a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a>. <a href="/wiki/Grimsby_Town_railway_station" title="Grimsby Town railway station">Grimsby</a> is connected (also through Scunthorpe) on <a href="/wiki/TransPennine_Express" title="TransPennine Express">TransPennine Express</a>' South TransPennine route from Sheffield (originating at <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Airport railway station">Manchester Airport</a>).
</p><p><br />
</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="High-speed rail in the United Kingdom">High-speed rail in the United Kingdom</a></div>
<p>The region is home to a rail land speed record. On 1 November 1987, an <a href="/wiki/InterCity_125" title="InterCity 125">InterCity 125</a> travelled at 238&#160;km/h between <a href="/wiki/Northallerton_railway_station" title="Northallerton railway station">Northallerton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thirsk_railway_station" title="Thirsk railway station">Thirsk</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mass_transit">Mass transit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yorkshire_and_the_Humber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Mass transit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_tram_at_Hillsborough_-_geograph.org.uk_-_811984.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Sheffield_tram_at_Hillsborough_-_geograph.org.uk_-_811984.jpg/220px-Sheffield_tram_at_Hillsborough_-_geograph.org.uk_-_811984.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Sheffield_tram_at_Hillsborough_-_geograph.org.uk_-_811984.jpg/330px-Sheffield_tram_at_Hillsborough_-_geograph.org.uk_-_811984.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Sheffield_tram_at_Hillsborough_-_geograph.org.uk_-_811984.jpg/440px-Sheffield_tram_at_Hillsborough_-_geograph.org.uk_-_811984.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="409" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sheffield_tram_at_Hillsborough_-_geograph.org.uk_-_811984.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Supertram" title="Sheffield Supertram">Sheffield Supertram</a> in 1998</div></div></div>
<p>Only Sheffield has its own mass-transit system, the <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Supertram" title="Sheffield Supertram">Sheffield Supertram</a>, owned by SYPTE and run by <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_Sheffield" title="Stagecoach Sheffield">Stagecoach</a>. Leeds and Bradford have more developed commuter rail systems but lack any mass transit system. The <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Supertram" title="Leeds Supertram">Leeds Supertram</a> was an approved scheme in Leeds. However, the funding was pulled and the scheme has been replaced by the proposed <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Trolleybus" class="mw-redirect" title="Leeds Trolleybus">Leeds Trolleybus</a> scheme. In the past Bradford, Halifax, Huddersfield, Kingston upon Hull, Leeds, Rotherham, Sheffield and York have all had mass-transit systems.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air">Air</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yorkshire_and_the_Humber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Air">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_Bradford_International_Airport_terminal,_left.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Leeds_Bradford_International_Airport_terminal%2C_left.jpg/220px-Leeds_Bradford_International_Airport_terminal%2C_left.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Leeds_Bradford_International_Airport_terminal%2C_left.jpg/330px-Leeds_Bradford_International_Airport_terminal%2C_left.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Leeds_Bradford_International_Airport_terminal%2C_left.jpg/440px-Leeds_Bradford_International_Airport_terminal%2C_left.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Leeds_Bradford_International_Airport_terminal,_left.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Leeds_Bradford_Airport" title="Leeds Bradford Airport">Leeds Bradford Airport</a> is the busiest in the region.</div></div></div>
<p>Airports in the region are <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Bradford_Airport" title="Leeds Bradford Airport">Leeds Bradford Airport</a> at <a href="/wiki/Yeadon,_West_Yorkshire" title="Yeadon, West Yorkshire">Yeadon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doncaster_Sheffield_Airport" title="Doncaster Sheffield Airport">Doncaster Sheffield Airport</a> (which opened in April 2005 on the former <a href="/wiki/RAF_Finningley" title="RAF Finningley">RAF Finningley</a>) near <a href="/wiki/Doncaster" title="Doncaster">Doncaster</a> and <a href="/wiki/Humberside_Airport" title="Humberside Airport">Humberside Airport</a> (which opened in April 1974 on the former <a href="/wiki/RAF_Kirmington" title="RAF Kirmington">RAF Kirmington</a>) near <a href="/wiki/Brigg" title="Brigg">Brigg</a> in <a href="/wiki/North_Lincolnshire" title="North Lincolnshire">North Lincolnshire</a>. Leeds Bradford Airport is the largest in the region by passenger numbers, Robin Hood boasts the longest runway (2.7&#160;km) of any airport in the region and Humberside Airport boasts an active heliport. <a href="/wiki/Jet2.com" title="Jet2.com">Jet2.com</a>, a popular low-cost airline at Leeds Bradford has around fifty <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737" title="Boeing 737">Boeing 737</a> aircraft.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sheffield_City_Airport" title="Sheffield City Airport">Sheffield City Airport</a> formerly served the city of Sheffield. However, the airport struggled to attract many scheduled services and closed following the opening of Robin Hood Doncaster Sheffield Airport.
</p><p>Lying outside of the region <a href="/wiki/Durham_Tees_Valley_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Durham Tees Valley Airport">Durham Tees Valley Airport</a> (former <a href="/wiki/RAF_Middleton_St._George" class="mw-redirect" title="RAF Middleton St. George">RAF Middleton St. George</a>) serves the northernmost areas of the region, being next to the River Tees, and less than a mile from <a href="/wiki/Over_Dinsdale" title="Over Dinsdale">Over Dinsdale</a> on <a href="/wiki/North_Yorkshire" title="North Yorkshire">North Yorkshire</a>'s northern edge. There are day and night <a href="/wiki/TransPennine_Express" title="TransPennine Express">direct rail connections</a> from the region to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/National_Express_Coaches" title="National Express Coaches">National Express</a> coach services also run directly to <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">Heathrow Airport</a> from the region.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Water">Water</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yorkshire_and_the_Humber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Water">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fertiliser,_Farming_and_Ferry_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1737437.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Fertiliser%2C_Farming_and_Ferry_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1737437.jpg/220px-Fertiliser%2C_Farming_and_Ferry_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1737437.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Fertiliser%2C_Farming_and_Ferry_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1737437.jpg/330px-Fertiliser%2C_Farming_and_Ferry_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1737437.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Fertiliser%2C_Farming_and_Ferry_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1737437.jpg/440px-Fertiliser%2C_Farming_and_Ferry_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1737437.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3282" data-file-height="2424" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fertiliser,_Farming_and_Ferry_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1737437.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Pride of York (<a href="/wiki/MS_Norsea" class="mw-redirect" title="MS Norsea">MS Norsea</a>) ferry, which operates from <a href="/wiki/Kingston_upon_Hull" title="Kingston upon Hull">Hull</a>, in March 2010; the service to Rotterdam began in August 1965 and the service to Gothenburg (<i>Göteborg</i>) started in March 1966</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Kingston_upon_Hull" title="Kingston upon Hull">Hull</a> has daily <a href="/wiki/P%26O_Ferries" title="P&amp;O Ferries">ferries</a> (former <a href="/wiki/North_Sea_Ferries" title="North Sea Ferries">North Sea Ferries</a>) to <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Bruges-Zeebrugge" class="mw-redirect" title="Port of Bruges-Zeebrugge">Zeebrugge</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rotterdam" title="Rotterdam">Rotterdam</a> (<a href="/wiki/Europoort" title="Europoort">Europoort</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Hull also has a large freight port and an active fishing port. <a href="/wiki/Immingham" title="Immingham">Immingham</a> carries much freight transport via <a href="/wiki/DFDS_Tor_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="DFDS Tor Line">DFDS Tor Line</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Stena_Line" title="Stena Line">Stena Line</a>. <a href="/wiki/Goole" title="Goole">Goole</a> is Britain's most inland port and is used mostly for importing commodities such as <a href="/wiki/Coal" title="Coal">coal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timber" class="mw-redirect" title="Timber">timber</a>.
</p><p>The region also has a canal network. The <a href="/wiki/Leeds_and_Liverpool_Canal" title="Leeds and Liverpool Canal">Leeds and Liverpool Canal</a> links West Yorkshire with the North West and the <a href="/wiki/Aire_and_Calder_Navigation" title="Aire and Calder Navigation">Aire and Calder Navigation</a> links Leeds and the coal fields of West and North Yorkshire with the ports to the East of the region.  There are also several smaller canals in the region, often built for quite specific purposes.  Many stretches of the smaller canals in the region have been backfilled. The steepest locks in Britain are at Bingley – <a href="/wiki/Bingley_Five_Rise_Locks" title="Bingley Five Rise Locks">Bingley Five Rise Locks</a>, built by <a href="/wiki/John_Longbotham" title="John Longbotham">John Longbotham</a>, who designed the canal.
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yorkshire_and_the_Humber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Cloud_Factory_-_geograph.org.uk_-_349038.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/The_Cloud_Factory_-_geograph.org.uk_-_349038.jpg/220px-The_Cloud_Factory_-_geograph.org.uk_-_349038.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/The_Cloud_Factory_-_geograph.org.uk_-_349038.jpg/330px-The_Cloud_Factory_-_geograph.org.uk_-_349038.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/The_Cloud_Factory_-_geograph.org.uk_-_349038.jpg/440px-The_Cloud_Factory_-_geograph.org.uk_-_349038.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="338" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Cloud_Factory_-_geograph.org.uk_-_349038.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 4GW <a href="/wiki/Drax_power_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Drax power station">Drax power station</a>'s 850 foot chimney, built in May 1969, is the tallest in the UK; the power station burns 10 million tonnes of coal a year, via 30 trains a day. It has the second-largest electricity output in <a href="/wiki/Category:Electric_power_in_the_European_Union" title="Category:Electric power in the European Union">western Europe</a>, after <a href="/wiki/Neurath_Power_Station" title="Neurath Power Station">Neurath Power Station</a> in western Germany</div></div></div>
<p>Until 2011, <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Forward" title="Yorkshire Forward">Yorkshire Forward</a> was the <a href="/wiki/Regional_Development_Agency" class="mw-redirect" title="Regional Development Agency">Regional Development Agency</a> charged with improving the Yorkshire and Humber economy, where some 270,000 businesses contribute to an economy worth in excess of £80&#160;billion. With over 5&#160;million people living in the region it ranks alongside some small countries including Ireland, Greece, Norway and Singapore.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The region has the second lowest rate of <a href="/wiki/Gross_value_added" title="Gross value added">GVA</a> in England. However, Leeds has a much higher average GVA than most of South Yorkshire. <a href="/wiki/Business_Link" title="Business Link">Business Link</a> Yorkshire<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> until November 2011 was on the Capitol Business Park in <a href="/wiki/Dodworth" title="Dodworth">Dodworth</a>, west of the M1 near <a href="/wiki/Barnsley" title="Barnsley">Barnsley</a> near the bypass (<a href="/wiki/A628_road" title="A628 road">A628</a>). The region's <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing_Advisory_Service" title="Manufacturing Advisory Service">Manufacturing Advisory Service</a><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> was until March 2016 at Saint Martins House in <a href="/wiki/Potternewton" title="Potternewton">Potternewton</a> next to <a href="/wiki/Chapel_Allerton_Hospital" title="Chapel Allerton Hospital">Chapel Allerton Hospital</a>, on the former A61, with two other offices at the <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Manufacturing_Park" title="Advanced Manufacturing Park">Advanced Manufacturing Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catcliffe" title="Catcliffe">Catcliffe</a> off the <a href="/wiki/A630_road" title="A630 road">A630</a> <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Parkway" title="Sheffield Parkway">Sheffield Parkway</a>, and also on <i>St. Georges Road</i> in the west of Hull; the functions are now represented by the organisation <a href="/w/index.php?title=Made_in_Yorkshire&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Made in Yorkshire (page does not exist)">Made in Yorkshire</a>. The <a href="/wiki/UK_Trade_%26_Investment" title="UK Trade &amp; Investment">UKTI</a> office for the region was off the <a href="/wiki/A653_road" class="mw-redirect" title="A653 road">A653</a>, directly south of Bridgewater Place in <a href="/wiki/Holbeck" title="Holbeck">Holbeck</a>, and its successor (in July 2016) <a href="/wiki/Department_for_International_Trade" title="Department for International Trade">DIT</a> Yorkshire and the Humber is at the Digital Media Centre near <a href="/wiki/Barnsley_Interchange" title="Barnsley Interchange">Barnsley Interchange</a>, run by Mark Robson.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/NHS_Yorkshire_and_the_Humber" class="mw-redirect" title="NHS Yorkshire and the Humber">NHS Yorkshire and the Humber</a>, the regional <a href="/wiki/NHS_strategic_health_authority" class="mw-redirect" title="NHS strategic health authority">strategic health authority</a>, was at the roundabout at the bottom of <i>Kirkstall Road</i> in Leeds, with another office in the north of Sheffield. The charity-funded <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Air_Ambulance" title="Yorkshire Air Ambulance">Yorkshire Air Ambulance</a>, established in October 2000, is based at <a href="/wiki/Nostell_Priory" title="Nostell Priory">Nostell Priory</a> south-east of Wakefield on the A638 (previously at Leeds Bradford Airport) and <a href="/wiki/RAF_Topcliffe" title="RAF Topcliffe">RAF Topcliffe</a> (previously until 2012 at <a href="/wiki/Bagby" title="Bagby">Bagby</a> near Thirsk); the helicopter can land on the main hospitals' roofs. The state-funded <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Ambulance_Service" title="Yorkshire Ambulance Service">Yorkshire Ambulance Service</a> is based next to Coca-Cola on the Wakefield 41 Business Park, near the A650. <a href="/wiki/NHS_Blood_and_Transplant" title="NHS Blood and Transplant">National Blood Service</a> for the area is off the <a href="/wiki/A6102_road" class="mw-redirect" title="A6102 road">A6102</a> in the north of Sheffield, at the west end of the <a href="/wiki/Northern_General_Hospital" title="Northern General Hospital">Northern General Hospital</a>.
</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Mining_in_South_Yorkshire" title="Category:Mining in South Yorkshire">Category:Mining in South Yorkshire</a></div>
<p>Yorkshire in the past has been synonymous with <a href="/wiki/Coal_mining_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Coal mining in the United Kingdom">coal mining</a>. Many pits closed in the 1990s, with the last two that were open in the Pontefract area at <a href="/wiki/Kellingley_Colliery" title="Kellingley Colliery">Kellingley</a> (closed on 18 December 2015) and <a href="/wiki/Sharlston,_West_Yorkshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Sharlston, West Yorkshire">Sharlston</a>. In South Yorkshire, there was <a href="/wiki/Maltby_Main_Colliery" title="Maltby Main Colliery">Maltby Main Colliery</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hatfield_Colliery" title="Hatfield Colliery">Hatfield Colliery</a> (closed in June 2015) at <a href="/wiki/Stainforth,_South_Yorkshire" title="Stainforth, South Yorkshire">Stainforth</a>. The <a href="/wiki/National_Union_of_Mineworkers_(Great_Britain)" title="National Union of Mineworkers (Great Britain)">NUM</a> was very Yorkshire-dominated. Coal still plays a part in the economy – there are two large power stations along the <a href="/wiki/River_Aire" title="River Aire">Aire</a> Valley, with Drax being the second largest in Europe with 3,945&#160;<a href="/wiki/Megawatt" class="mw-redirect" title="Megawatt">MW</a> of capacity, and Eggborough which is owned by the Czech Republic's <a href="/wiki/Energetick%C3%BD_a_pr%C5%AFmyslov%C3%BD_holding" title="Energetický a průmyslový holding">Energetický a průmyslový holding</a> (EPH) since 2014 and was owned by <a href="/wiki/British_Energy" title="British Energy">British Energy</a> until 2010; Ferrybridge C closed on 23 March 2016. The <a href="/wiki/Electricity_distribution" class="mw-redirect" title="Electricity distribution">distribution</a> <a href="/wiki/Distribution_Network_Operator" class="mw-redirect" title="Distribution Network Operator">area</a> once looked after by the <a href="/wiki/Regional_electricity_company" class="mw-redirect" title="Regional electricity company">regional electricity company</a> <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Electricity" title="Yorkshire Electricity">Yorkshire Electricity</a> is now looked after by <a href="/wiki/Northern_Powergrid" title="Northern Powergrid">Northern Powergrid</a> (former YEDL), owned by <a href="/wiki/Berkshire_Hathaway" title="Berkshire Hathaway">Berkshire Hathaway</a> (since 2001) of <a href="/wiki/Omaha,_Nebraska" title="Omaha, Nebraska">Omaha, Nebraska</a>. The supply side of the region is now owned by <a href="/wiki/Npower_(United_Kingdom)" title="Npower (United Kingdom)">npower</a> (former <a href="/wiki/National_Power" title="National Power">National Power</a>, now owned by <a href="/wiki/RWE" title="RWE">RWE</a> of <a href="/wiki/Essen" title="Essen">Essen</a>, Germany). 29% of the UK's oil is refined on the Humber.
</p>

<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Thyrbergh_Hydro&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Thyrbergh Hydro (page does not exist)">Thrybergh</a></li></ul>
</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%;font-weight:normal;">Proposed/Future</th><td class="navbox-list navbox-even" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px"><div style="padding:0em 0.25em"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Naburn_Hydro&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Naburn Hydro (page does not exist)">Naburn</a></div></td></tr></tbody></table><div></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%"><a href="/wiki/Incinerator" class="mw-redirect" title="Incinerator">Incinerators</a><br />/<a href="/wiki/Waste-to-energy" title="Waste-to-energy">Waste</a></th><td class="navbox-list navbox-odd" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px"><div style="padding:0em 0.25em"></div><table class="nowraplinks navbox-subgroup" style="border-spacing:0"><tbody><tr><th scope="row" class="navbox-group" style="width:1%;font-weight:normal;">Active</th><td class="navbox-list navbox-odd" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px"><div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
