Tangerine Confectionery (Lion Confectionery) is on the <a href="/wiki/A643_road" title="A643 road">A643</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Status_International&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Status International (page does not exist)">Status International</a> UK (<a href="/wiki/Electric_light" title="Electric light">lightbulbs</a>) is in the centre of Cleckheaton. Mars Complementary Petcare is off the A62 on the Oakwell Way Ind Estate at Birstall, next to <a href="/wiki/Birstall_Shopping_Park" title="Birstall Shopping Park">Birstall Shopping Park</a>; nearby is <a href="/wiki/Pitchero" title="Pitchero">Pitchero</a>, a sports website firm. <a href="/wiki/Poundstretcher" title="Poundstretcher">Poundstretcher</a> is in <a href="/wiki/Deighton,_West_Yorkshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Deighton, West Yorkshire">Deighton</a> east of Huddersfield.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Entrance_to_Syngenta_chemical_works,_Leeds_Road,_Deighton,_Huddersfield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_382001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Entrance_to_Syngenta_chemical_works%2C_Leeds_Road%2C_Deighton%2C_Huddersfield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_382001.jpg/220px-Entrance_to_Syngenta_chemical_works%2C_Leeds_Road%2C_Deighton%2C_Huddersfield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_382001.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Entrance_to_Syngenta_chemical_works%2C_Leeds_Road%2C_Deighton%2C_Huddersfield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_382001.jpg/330px-Entrance_to_Syngenta_chemical_works%2C_Leeds_Road%2C_Deighton%2C_Huddersfield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_382001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Entrance_to_Syngenta_chemical_works%2C_Leeds_Road%2C_Deighton%2C_Huddersfield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_382001.jpg/440px-Entrance_to_Syngenta_chemical_works%2C_Leeds_Road%2C_Deighton%2C_Huddersfield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_382001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="464" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Entrance_to_Syngenta_chemical_works,_Leeds_Road,_Deighton,_Huddersfield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_382001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Syngenta (former <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Chemical_Industries" title="Imperial Chemical Industries">ICI Organics</a>, then <a href="/wiki/Zeneca" title="Zeneca">Zeneca</a> Agrochemicals until 1993) works on the <a href="/wiki/A62_road" title="A62 road">A62</a> in Huddersfield; it makes <a href="/wiki/Herbicide" title="Herbicide">herbicides</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cyhalothrin" title="Cyhalothrin">cyhalothrin</a> insecticide</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/David_Brown_Ltd." title="David Brown Ltd.">David Brown Ltd.</a> is in <a href="/wiki/Lockwood,_West_Yorkshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Lockwood, West Yorkshire">Lockwood</a> in Huddersfield; this company owned <a href="/wiki/Aston_Martin" title="Aston Martin">Aston Martin</a> from 1947 to 1972 and the company is now part of <a href="/wiki/Textron" title="Textron">Textron</a>. In Huddersfield are <a href="/wiki/Cummins" title="Cummins">Cummins Turbo Technologies</a> (former <a href="/wiki/Holset_Engineering" class="mw-redirect" title="Holset Engineering">Holset</a>) who make <a href="/wiki/Turbocharger" title="Turbocharger">turbochargers</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=VTL_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="VTL Group (page does not exist)">VTL Group</a> make automotive components, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Fired_Up_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Fired Up Group (page does not exist)">Fired Up Group</a> who own <a href="/w/index.php?title=Armco_Security&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Armco Security (page does not exist)">Armco Security</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Corby_of_Windsor&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Corby of Windsor (page does not exist)">Corby of Windsor</a> (<a href="/wiki/Trouser_press" title="Trouser press">trouser press</a>), <a href="/w/index.php?title=Brook_Crompton&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Brook Crompton (page does not exist)">Brook Crompton</a> (<a href="/wiki/Electric_motor" title="Electric motor">electric motors</a>) and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Graham_Group_(company)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Graham Group (company) (page does not exist)">Graham Group</a> (plumbing retail). To the east of Fired Up is <a href="/w/index.php?title=Britannia_Rescue&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Britannia Rescue (page does not exist)">Britannia Rescue</a> (owned by <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Victoria" title="Liverpool Victoria">LV</a>) at the <a href="/wiki/A616_road" title="A616 road">A616</a>/B6432 junction. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Broadbent_(company)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Broadbent (company) (page does not exist)">Broadbent</a>, make industrial centrifuges in central Huddersfield. Many fabric companies are in Huddersfield and the surrounding areas; <a href="/w/index.php?title=Taylor_%26_Lodge&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Taylor &amp; Lodge (page does not exist)">Taylor &amp; Lodge</a>, owned by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bulmer_%26_Lumb&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bulmer &amp; Lumb (page does not exist)">Bulmer &amp; Lumb</a> of Bradford, wove cloth for the <a href="/wiki/Wedding_of_Prince_William_and_Catherine_Middleton" title="Wedding of Prince William and Catherine Middleton">2011 Royal Wedding</a>; <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dugdale_Bros_%26_Co&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dugdale Bros &amp; Co (page does not exist)">Dugdale Bros &amp; Co</a> are in the centre. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Novaglaze&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Novaglaze (page does not exist)">Novaglaze</a> produced the glass for the <a href="/wiki/London_Eye" title="London Eye">London Eye</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Trojan_Plastics&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Trojan Plastics (page does not exist)">Trojan Plastics</a> is the UK's largest bath manufacturer in <a href="/wiki/Milnsbridge" title="Milnsbridge">Milnsbridge</a> in west Huddersfield next to the River Colne. <a href="/wiki/Thornton_%26_Ross" title="Thornton &amp; Ross">Thornton &amp; Ross</a> healthcare is on the A62 next to the <a href="/wiki/River_Colne,_West_Yorkshire" title="River Colne, West Yorkshire">River Colne</a> in <a href="/wiki/Linthwaite" title="Linthwaite">Linthwaite</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dathan_Tool_%26_Gauge&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dathan Tool &amp; Gauge (page does not exist)">Dathan Tool &amp; Gauge</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cutting_tool_(machining)" title="Cutting tool (machining)">cutting tools</a>) are in Meltham. <a href="/w/index.php?title=John_Cotton_(company)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="John Cotton (company) (page does not exist)">John Cotton</a> at the A62/A644 junction in Mirfield are Europe's largest producer of <a href="/wiki/Duvet" title="Duvet">duvets</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Camira_Fabrics&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Camira Fabrics (page does not exist)">Camira Fabrics</a> (fabrics for public transport) is based at Hopton Mills, south of Mirfield, with a manufacturing site off the B6108 in the east of Meltham, and makes the upholstery for London buses; further north next to River Calder is a site of <a href="/wiki/Dr._Reddy%27s_Laboratories" title="Dr. Reddy&#39;s Laboratories">Dr. Reddy's Laboratories</a> in the south of Mirfield. Overlooked by the Emley Moor tower at the <i>Grange Moor Roundabout</i> off the <a href="/wiki/A637_road" class="mw-redirect" title="A637 road">A637</a> and <a href="/wiki/A642_road" title="A642 road">A642</a> (towards Wakefield) at <a href="/wiki/Grange_Moor" title="Grange Moor">Grange Moor</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kirkburton" title="Kirkburton">Kirkburton</a> is <a href="/wiki/Bonmarch%C3%A9" title="Bonmarché">Bonmarché</a>, previously owned by <a href="/wiki/Peacocks_(clothing)" title="Peacocks (clothing)">Peacocks</a> until 2012.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Haribo_Sweets_Factory_-_Sessions_House_Yard_-_geograph.org.uk_-_576986.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Haribo_Sweets_Factory_-_Sessions_House_Yard_-_geograph.org.uk_-_576986.jpg/220px-Haribo_Sweets_Factory_-_Sessions_House_Yard_-_geograph.org.uk_-_576986.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Haribo_Sweets_Factory_-_Sessions_House_Yard_-_geograph.org.uk_-_576986.jpg/330px-Haribo_Sweets_Factory_-_Sessions_House_Yard_-_geograph.org.uk_-_576986.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Haribo_Sweets_Factory_-_Sessions_House_Yard_-_geograph.org.uk_-_576986.jpg/440px-Haribo_Sweets_Factory_-_Sessions_House_Yard_-_geograph.org.uk_-_576986.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="432" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Haribo_Sweets_Factory_-_Sessions_House_Yard_-_geograph.org.uk_-_576986.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Haribo factory in Pontefract on the A639 in the centre of the town near <a href="/wiki/Pontefract_Tanshelf_railway_station" title="Pontefract Tanshelf railway station">Tanshelf</a> station</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Hickson_%26_Welch" title="Hickson &amp; Welch">Hickson &amp; Welch</a> (owned by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Arch_Chemicals&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Arch Chemicals (page does not exist)">Arch Chemicals</a>) were in <a href="/wiki/Castleford" title="Castleford">Castleford</a> and closed in 2005. <a href="/wiki/Netto_UK" title="Netto UK">Netto UK</a> (previously owned by Asda) was in <a href="/wiki/South_Elmsall" title="South Elmsall">South Elmsall</a> until 2011. Nestle made <a href="/wiki/Toffee_Crisp" class="mw-redirect" title="Toffee Crisp">Toffee Crisp</a> and <a href="/wiki/After_Eight" title="After Eight">After Eight</a> in <a href="/wiki/Castleford" title="Castleford">Castleford</a> until 2012 then made in Halifax, and <a href="/wiki/Haribo" title="Haribo">Haribo</a> makes liquorice and <a href="/wiki/Pontefract_cake" title="Pontefract cake">Pontefract cakes</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pontefract" title="Pontefract">Pontefract</a>. <a href="/wiki/Burberry" title="Burberry">Burberry</a> had a main clothing factory in Castleford until the end of 2015, which is planned to move to Leeds. Cott Beverages are between the A645 and the <a href="/wiki/Dearne_Valley_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Dearne Valley Line">railway</a> in the east of Pontefract (former <a href="/w/index.php?title=Benjamin_Shaw_%26_Sons&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Benjamin Shaw &amp; Sons (page does not exist)">Benjamin Shaw &amp; Sons</a> before 2006); <a href="/wiki/Tangerine_Confectionery" title="Tangerine Confectionery">Tangerine Confectionery</a> (former Cadbury-owned <a href="/wiki/Monkhill_Confectionery" class="mw-redirect" title="Monkhill Confectionery">Monkhill Confectionery</a>) make <a href="/wiki/Butterkist" title="Butterkist">Butterkist</a> (the UK's best-selling) popcorn north of Cott Beverages, near <a href="/wiki/Pontefract_Monkhill_railway_station" title="Pontefract Monkhill railway station">Pontefract Monkhill railway station</a>, on the site which claims to be the birthplace of liquorice. <a href="/wiki/Ardagh_Group" title="Ardagh Group">Ardagh Glass UK</a> is in the south of <a href="/wiki/Knottingley" title="Knottingley">Knottingley</a>, with sites at <a href="/wiki/Monk_Bretton" title="Monk Bretton">Monk Bretton</a> and Wheatley (Doncaster). <a href="/wiki/St%C3%B6lzle_Glass" title="Stölzle Glass">Stölzle Flaconnage</a> (former Bagley's before 1994) makes <a href="/wiki/Container_glass" title="Container glass">glass containers</a>, between the A645 and the <a href="/wiki/Aire_and_Calder_Navigation" title="Aire and Calder Navigation">Aire and Calder Navigation</a>, and further along the A645, <a href="/wiki/Tradebe" title="Tradebe">Tradebe</a> recycle solvents. <a href="/wiki/Total_S.A." title="Total S.A.">Total</a> Lubricants UK is in Knottingley (Ferrybridge Hill) on the B6136. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Plasmor&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Plasmor (page does not exist)">Plasmor</a> (concrete) is in the south-east of Knottingley, with a large site at <a href="/wiki/Great_Heck" title="Great Heck">Great Heck</a> next to a <a href="/wiki/RAF_Snaith" title="RAF Snaith">former airfield</a> where <a href="/w/index.php?title=H%2BH&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="H+H (page does not exist)">H+H</a> (Danish) make <a href="/wiki/Autoclaved_aerated_concrete" title="Autoclaved aerated concrete">aircrete</a>; both sites imported <a href="/wiki/Pulverised_fuel_ash" class="mw-redirect" title="Pulverised fuel ash">pulverised fuel ash</a> (PFA) from the former Eggborough power station; in east Knottingley, off the A645, Croda Hydrocarbons (bitumen) closed in 2008.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Moon_river_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1007988.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Moon_river_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1007988.jpg/220px-Moon_river_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1007988.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="303" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Moon_river_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1007988.jpg/330px-Moon_river_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1007988.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Moon_river_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1007988.jpg/440px-Moon_river_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1007988.jpg 2x" data-file-width="465" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Moon_river_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1007988.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Former Castleford Nestlé factory in 2008</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Teva_Pharmaceutical_Industries" title="Teva Pharmaceutical Industries">Teva Pharmaceutical Industries</a> UK is next to the M62 at Castleford, near <a href="/wiki/Glasshoughton_railway_station" title="Glasshoughton railway station">Glasshoughton railway station</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=LPA_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="LPA Group (page does not exist)">LPA Group</a> off the <a href="/wiki/A655_road" class="mw-redirect" title="A655 road">A655</a> in Hopetown, <a href="/wiki/Normanton,_West_Yorkshire" title="Normanton, West Yorkshire">Normanton</a> makes <a href="/wiki/LED_lamp" title="LED lamp">LED lighting</a> for trains; <a href="/wiki/Poundworld" title="Poundworld">Poundworld</a> was founded on a Wakefield market in 1974, and the family-owned company has 240 shops. To the west, Napier Brown (part of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Real_Good_Food&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Real Good Food (page does not exist)">Real Good Food</a>) makes <a href="/wiki/Whitworths" title="Whitworths">Whitworths</a>' sugar in Hopetown. On the other side of the M62 (junction 31) in <a href="/w/index.php?title=Whitwood&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Whitwood (page does not exist)">Whitwood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pioneer_Corporation" title="Pioneer Corporation">Pioneer Technology UK</a> closed their large plasma TV factory in March 2009. <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_Enterprises" title="Coca-Cola Enterprises">Coca-Cola UK</a> claim to have the largest <a href="/wiki/CCE_Wakefield" title="CCE Wakefield">soft drinks factory</a> in the world at its 41-acre site, with 71,000 sq metres of buildings, at <a href="/wiki/Outwood,_West_Yorkshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Outwood, West Yorkshire">Outwood</a>, which was built in 1989, and produces 6,000 cans (over 100 cans a second, on three canning lines) and 3,300 bottles a minute (seven <a href="/wiki/Polyethylene_terephthalate" title="Polyethylene terephthalate">PET</a> bottling lines, the fastest 2 litre bottling plant in the world), producing 100&#160;million cases of soft drinks a year; the bottle caps are made out of <a href="/wiki/High-density_polyethylene" title="High-density polyethylene">HDPE</a>. To keep up with supply, <a href="/wiki/Rexam" title="Rexam">Rexam</a> have a can factory next door. Nearby is the headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Card_Factory" title="Card Factory">Card Factory</a>, with over 800 shops is Britain's biggest card shop chain and started in 1997; opposite is the <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Purchasing_Organisation" title="Yorkshire Purchasing Organisation">Yorkshire Purchasing Organisation</a>, which buys stock for most of the region's metropolitan boroughs and North Yorkshire, on south-west side of Wakefield 41. On the other side of the roundabout is <a href="/wiki/Mitre_Sports_International" title="Mitre Sports International">Mitre Sports International</a>. Morrisons have their <a href="/wiki/Rathbones_Bakeries" title="Rathbones Bakeries">Rathbones Bakeries</a> on Wakefield 41.
</p><p><a href="/w/index.php?title=Group_Rhodes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Group Rhodes (page does not exist)">Group Rhodes</a> off the <a href="/wiki/A638_road" title="A638 road">A638</a> in east Wakefield, make <a href="/w/index.php?title=Machine_cell&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Machine cell (page does not exist)">machine cells</a>. On the <a href="/wiki/Flanshaw" title="Flanshaw">Flanshaw</a> Ind Est in west Wakefield is <a href="/wiki/Technal" title="Technal">Technal</a> (aluminium facades) and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wicona&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Wicona (page does not exist)">Wicona</a>, part of <a href="/wiki/Norsk_Hydro" title="Norsk Hydro">Norsk Hydro</a>. Bombardier built trains at <a href="/wiki/Horbury_railway_works" title="Horbury railway works">Horbury</a> until 2006 where they made <a href="/wiki/CrossCountry" title="CrossCountry">CrossCountry</a>'s <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_221" title="British Rail Class 221">Class 221</a> <i>Super Voyager</i> and <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_220" title="British Rail Class 220">Class 220</a> <i>Voyager</i> (and were also assembled at the <a href="/wiki/La_Brugeoise_et_Nivelles" title="La Brugeoise et Nivelles">BN</a> plant in Bruges, Belgium and Crespin in France, the former <a href="/wiki/ANF_Industrie" title="ANF Industrie">ANF Industrie</a>). <a href="/wiki/Northern_Foods" title="Northern Foods">Northern Foods</a> are now based at Trinity Business Park off the <a href="/wiki/A636_road" title="A636 road">A636</a> south of Wakefield town centre. Wakefield Shirt Group is next to the River Calder. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Double_TWO&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Double TWO (page does not exist)">Double TWO</a> shirts are based off the A638 in central Wakefield. <a href="/wiki/Nooter/Eriksen" title="Nooter/Eriksen">Nooter/Eriksen</a> UK is off the <a href="/wiki/A636_road" title="A636 road">A636</a> next to <a href="/wiki/Denby_Dale_railway_station" title="Denby Dale railway station">Denby Dale railway station</a>, and produce <a href="/wiki/Heat_recovery_steam_generator" title="Heat recovery steam generator">heat recovery steam generator</a> (HRSGs)
</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Sheffield" title="Economy of Sheffield">Economy of Sheffield</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_in_Sheffield" title="List of companies in Sheffield">List of companies in Sheffield</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chesterfield_Special_Cylinders,_Meadowhall,_Sheffield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1303107.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Chesterfield_Special_Cylinders%2C_Meadowhall%2C_Sheffield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1303107.jpg/220px-Chesterfield_Special_Cylinders%2C_Meadowhall%2C_Sheffield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1303107.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Chesterfield_Special_Cylinders%2C_Meadowhall%2C_Sheffield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1303107.jpg/330px-Chesterfield_Special_Cylinders%2C_Meadowhall%2C_Sheffield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1303107.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Chesterfield_Special_Cylinders%2C_Meadowhall%2C_Sheffield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1303107.jpg/440px-Chesterfield_Special_Cylinders%2C_Meadowhall%2C_Sheffield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1303107.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chesterfield_Special_Cylinders,_Meadowhall,_Sheffield_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1303107.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chesterfield Special Cylinders, directly north of Meadowhall on the B6082, on the former site of the historic <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire_Engine_Company" title="Yorkshire Engine Company">Yorkshire Engine Company</a></div></div></div>
<p>Sheffield is known for its steel industry, which has declined in recent years. <a href="/wiki/Outokumpu" title="Outokumpu">Outokumpu</a> (former <a href="/wiki/British_Steel_(historic)" class="mw-redirect" title="British Steel (historic)">British Steel plc</a> Stainless) near the <a href="/wiki/Tinsley_Viaduct" title="Tinsley Viaduct">Tinsley Viaduct</a> make stainless steel, just north of the former airport, with access via the <a href="/wiki/A631_road" title="A631 road">A631</a>. Polestar is on the A631 in former Brinsworth, now in Sheffield (Tinsley).On the opposite side of the A631 is <a href="/w/index.php?title=Betafence&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Betafence (page does not exist)">Betafence</a> UK, part of the world's main fencing manufacturer, and its second biggest plant; near the start of the A631 is <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tuffnells_Parcel_Express&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tuffnells Parcel Express (page does not exist)">Tuffnells Parcel Express</a> (owned by <a href="/wiki/Connect_Group" title="Connect Group">Connect Group</a> since 2014). Nearby, Nederman UK make fume extraction equipment. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Durham_Duplex&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Durham Duplex (page does not exist)">Durham Duplex</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=High_Speed_and_Carbide&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="High Speed and Carbide (page does not exist)">High Speed and Carbide</a> make razor blades and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Machine_knife&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Machine knife (page does not exist)">industrial knives</a> on the B6082 in Wood Hill. Nearby <a href="/w/index.php?title=Davy_Markham&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Davy Markham (page does not exist)">Davy Markham</a> (owned by <a href="/w/index.php?title=IVRCL&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="IVRCL (page does not exist)">IVRCL</a>) on the A6102 at Darnall, fabricate steel and it has one of largest engineering workshops in western Europe. In the same area is <a href="/w/index.php?title=William_Cook_Cast_Products&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="William Cook Cast Products (page does not exist)">William Cook Cast Products</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gripple_factory.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Gripple_factory.jpg/220px-Gripple_factory.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Gripple_factory.jpg/330px-Gripple_factory.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Gripple_factory.jpg/440px-Gripple_factory.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gripple_factory.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gripple factory on the A6109 in <a href="/wiki/Burngreave" title="Burngreave">Burngreave</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/w/index.php?title=Egginton_(company)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Egginton (company) (page does not exist)">Egginton</a> make cutlery in <a href="/wiki/Netherthorpe,_Sheffield" title="Netherthorpe, Sheffield">Netherthorpe</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/St_Vincent%27s_Quarter" title="St Vincent&#39;s Quarter">St Vincent's Quarter</a> east of the Shalesmoor A61 roundabout, which owns <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ibberson&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ibberson (page does not exist)">Ibberson</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=George_Wostenholm&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="George Wostenholm (page does not exist)">George Wostenholm</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=William_Rodgers_(company)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="William Rodgers (company) (page does not exist)">William Rodgers</a> (who make the <a href="/wiki/Fairbairn%E2%80%93Sykes_fighting_knife" title="Fairbairn–Sykes fighting knife">Fairbairn–Sykes fighting knife</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Rodgers" class="mw-redirect" title="Joseph Rodgers">Joseph Rodgers</a>, the world's oldest brand of cutlery known for their pen-knives and <a href="/wiki/Combat_knife" title="Combat knife">military knives</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Magtec&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Magtec (page does not exist)">Magtec</a>, on the B6083 in <a href="/wiki/Brightside,_Sheffield" title="Brightside, Sheffield">Brightside</a> next to the River Don, makes diesel-electric <a href="/wiki/Hybrid_electric_vehicle" title="Hybrid electric vehicle">hybrid drive</a> systems that can be retro-fitted to vehicles. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Technicut&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Technicut (page does not exist)">Technicut</a> is the UK's market leader in rotary cutting tools on the A6178 in Brightside. <a href="/wiki/Arconic" title="Arconic">Arconic</a> Forgings is at <a href="/wiki/Carbrook,_Sheffield" title="Carbrook, Sheffield">Carbrook</a> off the <a href="/wiki/A6102_road" class="mw-redirect" title="A6102 road">A6102</a>. <a href="/wiki/Gripple" title="Gripple">Gripple</a> make connectors for wire <a href="/wiki/Fence" title="Fence">fences</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Silverware&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="British Silverware (page does not exist)">British Silverware</a> is off the A6109, in the industrial area. <a href="/w/index.php?title=SCX_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="SCX Group (page does not exist)">SCX Group</a> in <a href="/wiki/Shiregreen_and_Brightside" title="Shiregreen and Brightside">Wincobank</a> built the rectractable-roof for the <a href="/wiki/No._1_Court_(Wimbledon)" title="No. 1 Court (Wimbledon)">No. 1 Court (Wimbledon)</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Polestar_(company)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Polestar (company) (page does not exist)">Polestar</a>, at Tinsley off the <a href="/wiki/A631_road" title="A631 road">A631</a> next to the M1, claim to have the most advanced <a href="/wiki/Rotogravure" title="Rotogravure">gravure printing</a> plant in Europe. Tinsley Bridge off the A631 makes <a href="/wiki/Suspension_(vehicle)" class="mw-redirect" title="Suspension (vehicle)">suspension</a> <a href="/wiki/Leaf_spring" title="Leaf spring">springs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Torsion_bar_suspension" title="Torsion bar suspension">torsion bars</a>. <a href="/wiki/SIG_plc" title="SIG plc">SIG plc</a> (Europe's largest insulation distributor) and <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Black_%26_Decker" title="Stanley Black &amp; Decker">Stanley Tools UK</a> are at the former <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_City_Airport_%26_Heliport" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheffield City Airport &amp; Heliport">city airport</a>, with a manufacturing plant off the A631 on the <a href="/wiki/Hellaby" title="Hellaby">Hellaby</a> Ind Estate next to the M18, and had a former site on the B6075 in Sheffield. <a href="/wiki/Siemens_VAI" class="mw-redirect" title="Siemens VAI">Siemens VAI</a> UK is on Sheffield Business Park near the former airport, with <a href="/w/index.php?title=EVO_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="EVO Group (page does not exist)">EVO Group</a>, who own the Banner stationery company, and <a href="/wiki/Ansys" title="Ansys">Ansys</a> (Fluent and CFX <a href="/wiki/Computational_fluid_dynamics" title="Computational fluid dynamics">CFD</a> software) has one of two main offices. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Go_Outdoors&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Go Outdoors (page does not exist)">Go Outdoors</a>, owned by <a href="/wiki/JD_Sports" title="JD Sports">JD Sports</a> since 2016, are in the south of Sheffield, near <a href="/wiki/Bramall_Lane" title="Bramall Lane">Bramall Lane</a> off the A61; Hi Gear Products, their brand is on the Boston Street Ind Est.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Geo._Bassett_%26_Co_confectionery_factory_in_Sheffield,_South_Yorkshire.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Geo._Bassett_%26_Co_confectionery_factory_in_Sheffield%2C_South_Yorkshire.jpg/220px-Geo._Bassett_%26_Co_confectionery_factory_in_Sheffield%2C_South_Yorkshire.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Geo._Bassett_%26_Co_confectionery_factory_in_Sheffield%2C_South_Yorkshire.jpg/330px-Geo._Bassett_%26_Co_confectionery_factory_in_Sheffield%2C_South_Yorkshire.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Geo._Bassett_%26_Co_confectionery_factory_in_Sheffield%2C_South_Yorkshire.jpg/440px-Geo._Bassett_%26_Co_confectionery_factory_in_Sheffield%2C_South_Yorkshire.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="426" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Geo._Bassett_%26_Co_confectionery_factory_in_Sheffield,_South_Yorkshire.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Cadbury_UK" class="mw-redirect" title="Cadbury UK">Cadbury Trebor Bassett</a> at the former <a href="/wiki/Bassett%27s" title="Bassett&#39;s">Bassett's</a> factory in <a href="/wiki/Owlerton" title="Owlerton">Owlerton</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cadbury_UK" class="mw-redirect" title="Cadbury UK">Cadbury UK</a> (formerly Bassett's) make <a href="/wiki/Liquorice_allsorts" title="Liquorice allsorts">liquorice allsorts</a> in the north of Sheffield on the <a href="/wiki/A61_road" title="A61 road">A61</a> next-door to <a href="/wiki/Owlerton_Stadium" title="Owlerton Stadium">Owlerton Stadium</a>; it is Cadbury's Gum &amp; Liquorice division, and also makes <a href="/wiki/Belvita" title="Belvita">Belvita</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oreo" title="Oreo">Oreo</a> for UK market. <a href="/wiki/Swann_Morton" title="Swann Morton">Swann Morton</a> is a world-leading manufacturer of <a href="/wiki/Scalpel" title="Scalpel">scalpel</a> blades and medical equipment at Owlerton opposite Bassetts on the A61. <a href="/wiki/Plusnet" title="Plusnet">Plusnet</a> (owned by <a href="/wiki/BT_Group" title="BT Group">BT</a>), <a href="/wiki/Learndirect" title="Learndirect">learndirect</a> (owned by Ufi Ltd), <a href="/wiki/Online_Centres_Network" title="Online Centres Network">Online Centres Network</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jobcentre_Plus" title="Jobcentre Plus">Jobcentre Plus</a> are in the city centre. Virgin Media have a main contact centre (former Telewest) directly south of Don Valley Stadium, and next to the tram line. <a href="/wiki/Spear_%26_Jackson" title="Spear &amp; Jackson">Spear &amp; Jackson</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Garden_tool" title="Garden tool">garden tool</a> company, are in the north of Sheffield. <a href="/wiki/B._Braun_Melsungen" title="B. Braun Melsungen">B. Braun Medical</a> is at <a href="/wiki/High_Green" title="High Green">High Green</a>, next to the <a href="/wiki/A616_road" title="A616 road">A616</a> roundabout in Chapeltown, and Ronseal (owned by <a href="/wiki/Sherwin-Williams" title="Sherwin-Williams">Sherwin-Williams</a>) is nearby further south on northern edge of Chapeltown. <a href="/w/index.php?title=MachineWorks&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="MachineWorks (page does not exist)">MachineWorks</a> in Sheffield is the leading developer of <a href="/wiki/Numerical_control" title="Numerical control">CNC</a> simulation on the B6069 near <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Botanical_Gardens" title="Sheffield Botanical Gardens">Sheffield Botanical Gardens</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Corus_Steelworks,_Rotherham_-_geograph.org.uk_-_787011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Corus_Steelworks%2C_Rotherham_-_geograph.org.uk_-_787011.jpg/220px-Corus_Steelworks%2C_Rotherham_-_geograph.org.uk_-_787011.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Corus_Steelworks%2C_Rotherham_-_geograph.org.uk_-_787011.jpg/330px-Corus_Steelworks%2C_Rotherham_-_geograph.org.uk_-_787011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Corus_Steelworks%2C_Rotherham_-_geograph.org.uk_-_787011.jpg/440px-Corus_Steelworks%2C_Rotherham_-_geograph.org.uk_-_787011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="427" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Corus_Steelworks,_Rotherham_-_geograph.org.uk_-_787011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Liberty_House_Group" title="Liberty House Group">Liberty Speciality Steels</a> Primary Mill continuous casting site in <a href="/wiki/Aldwarke" title="Aldwarke">Aldwarke</a> (Rotherham) in December 2007</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Rosebys" title="Rosebys">Rosebys</a> were in <a href="/wiki/Rotherham" title="Rotherham">Rotherham</a>, before 2008, and <a href="/wiki/KP_Snacks" title="KP Snacks">KP</a> make their nuts in Eastwood, to the north of the town. MTL Group, a steel fabrication company, is based off the <a href="/wiki/A631_road" title="A631 road">A631</a> in <a href="/wiki/Brinsworth" title="Brinsworth">Brinsworth</a> who claim to have the largest <a href="/wiki/Press_brake" title="Press brake">press brake</a> in the world (made by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ursviken_(company)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ursviken (company) (page does not exist)">Ursviken</a>). <a href="/wiki/Swinden_House" title="Swinden House">Swinden House</a> is home of Liberty Speciality Steels's main <a href="/w/index.php?title=Swinden_Technology_Centre&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Swinden Technology Centre (page does not exist)">Swinden Technology Centre</a>, its main R&amp;D centre in the UK, opposite <a href="/wiki/Rotherham_General_Hospital" title="Rotherham General Hospital">Rotherham General Hospital</a> on the <a href="/wiki/A618_road" class="mw-redirect" title="A618 road">A618</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Brinsworth_Strip_Mills&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Brinsworth Strip Mills (page does not exist)">Brinsworth Strip Mills</a>, run by Liberty Speciality Steels (former Corus Steel Narrow Strip), is opposite the Magna museum, south of the A6178, and makes narrow strip steel. The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Primary_Mill&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Primary Mill (page does not exist)">Primary Mill</a> makes steel billets and blooms – <a href="/wiki/Continuous_casting" title="Continuous casting">continuous casting</a> with an <a href="/wiki/Electric_arc_furnace" title="Electric arc furnace">electric arc furnace</a> with a melting shop, and is also known as Aldwarke Works. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Thrybergh_Mill&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Thrybergh Mill (page does not exist)">Thrybergh Mill</a> is east of the river off the A630, making steel bar, in a rolling mill. The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Brightbar_Mill&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Brightbar Mill (page does not exist)">Brightbar Mill</a> is off the A6123, on the west side of the railway next to Rawmarsh, making <a href="/wiki/Drawing_(manufacturing)" title="Drawing (manufacturing)">coiled bar</a>, in a rolling mill. These three sites around are known as <a href="/w/index.php?title=Rotherham_Works&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Rotherham Works (page does not exist)">Rotherham Works</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Beatson_Clark&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Beatson Clark (page does not exist)">Beatson Clark</a> (owned by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Newship_Group&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Newship Group (page does not exist)">Newship Group</a>) makes glass containers off the A6123 north of <a href="/wiki/Rotherham_Central_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Rotherham Central railway station">Rotherham Central railway station</a>.
</p><p><a href="/w/index.php?title=Dormer_Tools&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dormer Tools (page does not exist)">Dormer Tools</a> UK (owned by <a href="/wiki/Sandvik" title="Sandvik">Sandvik</a>) is on Waverley Business Park (Advanced Manufacturing Park) in <a href="/wiki/Catcliffe" title="Catcliffe">Catcliffe</a>, off the B6066 next to Morrisons. <a href="/w/index.php?title=LuK_GmbH&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="LuK GmbH (page does not exist)">LuK UK</a> (owned by the <a href="/wiki/Schaeffler_Group" title="Schaeffler Group">Schaeffler Group</a>) make <a href="/wiki/Clutch" title="Clutch">clutches</a> at <a href="/wiki/Wales,_South_Yorkshire" title="Wales, South Yorkshire">Wales</a>, south of <a href="/wiki/Aston,_South_Yorkshire" title="Aston, South Yorkshire">Aston</a> near the M1 junction 31 with the <a href="/wiki/A57_road" title="A57 road">A57</a>. <a href="/wiki/Jeld-Wen" title="Jeld-Wen">Jeld-Wen</a> UK (former <a href="/wiki/Boulton_%26_Paul_Ltd" title="Boulton &amp; Paul Ltd">Boulton &amp; Paul</a>) make doors on Swallownest Ind Est on the B6200 in <a href="/wiki/Aston_cum_Aughton" title="Aston cum Aughton">Aston cum Aughton</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Laycast&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Laycast (page does not exist)">Laycast</a> were nearby until November 2006, based off the B6200 at Aston cum Aughton, at which steel <a href="/wiki/Flywheel" title="Flywheel">flywheels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harmonic_oscillator" title="Harmonic oscillator">vibration dampers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Compacted_graphite_iron" title="Compacted graphite iron">compacted graphite iron</a> clutch plates were cast at its foundry. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Kiveton_Park_Steel&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Kiveton Park Steel (page does not exist)">Kiveton Park Steel</a> is on the B6059 next to <a href="/wiki/Kiveton_Park_railway_station" title="Kiveton Park railway station">Kiveton Park railway station</a>, mostly in <a href="/wiki/North_and_South_Anston" class="mw-redirect" title="North and South Anston">North and South Anston</a> (east of Wales).
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Zugstabsystem_Macalloy_in_Mariinsky_Theater.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Zugstabsystem_Macalloy_in_Mariinsky_Theater.jpg/150px-Zugstabsystem_Macalloy_in_Mariinsky_Theater.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="225" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Zugstabsystem_Macalloy_in_Mariinsky_Theater.jpg/225px-Zugstabsystem_Macalloy_in_Mariinsky_Theater.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Zugstabsystem_Macalloy_in_Mariinsky_Theater.jpg/300px-Zugstabsystem_Macalloy_in_Mariinsky_Theater.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="5184" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Zugstabsystem_Macalloy_in_Mariinsky_Theater.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Macalloy threaded tension bar at <a href="/wiki/Mariinsky_Theatre" title="Mariinsky Theatre">Mariinsky Theatre</a> in Russia</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Macalloy" title="Macalloy">Macalloy</a> in Dinnington is a world-leader in <a href="/wiki/Threading_(manufacturing)" title="Threading (manufacturing)">threaded</a> tension bar. Fresh-Pak Chilled Foods, off the A633 at Waterside Park, <a href="/wiki/Wombwell" title="Wombwell">Wombwell</a>, make most of the <a href="/wiki/Egg_salad" title="Egg salad">egg mayonnaise</a> (250&#160;tonnes a week) found in British sandwiches and for <a href="/wiki/Sandwich_filler" class="mw-redirect" title="Sandwich filler">sandwich fillers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Morphy_Richards" title="Morphy Richards">Morphy Richards</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roberts_Radio" title="Roberts Radio">Roberts Radio</a> are based between <a href="/wiki/Swinton,_South_Yorkshire" title="Swinton, South Yorkshire">Swinton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mexborough" title="Mexborough">Mexborough</a>. <a href="/wiki/Maplin_Electronics" class="mw-redirect" title="Maplin Electronics">Maplin Electronics</a> is based on the former site of <a href="/wiki/Manvers_Main_Colliery" title="Manvers Main Colliery">Manvers Main Colliery</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wath-upon-Dearne" class="mw-redirect" title="Wath-upon-Dearne">Wath-upon-Dearne</a>, off the A6023, with the call centre of <a href="/wiki/EE_Limited" title="EE Limited">EE</a> (former <a href="/wiki/Orange_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="Orange (UK)">Orange</a>) broadband next door. The <a href="/wiki/UK_Commission_for_Employment_and_Skills" title="UK Commission for Employment and Skills">UK Commission for Employment and Skills</a> (<a href="/wiki/Sector_Skills_Councils" class="mw-redirect" title="Sector Skills Councils">Sector Skills Councils</a>) is nearby, next to <a href="/wiki/Dearne_Valley_College" title="Dearne Valley College">Dearne Valley College</a>, which also looks after <a href="/wiki/Investors_in_People" title="Investors in People">Investors in People</a>. <a href="/wiki/Stelrad" title="Stelrad">Stelrad</a> in <a href="/wiki/Swinton,_South_Yorkshire" title="Swinton, South Yorkshire">Swinton Bridge</a> is the UK's largest producer of domestic <a href="/wiki/Radiator_(heating)" title="Radiator (heating)">radiators</a>, producing 2.5&#160;million a year, and Europe's leading radiator company, based off the A6022. MGB Plastics, on the A6123 in north Rotherham on Barbot Hall Ind Estate, are the UK's largest manufacturer of <a href="/wiki/Waste_container" title="Waste container">wheelie bins</a>, making around 1 million per year.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Site_preparation_for_new_warehouse._-_geograph.org.uk_-_481944.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Site_preparation_for_new_warehouse._-_geograph.org.uk_-_481944.jpg/220px-Site_preparation_for_new_warehouse._-_geograph.org.uk_-_481944.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Site_preparation_for_new_warehouse._-_geograph.org.uk_-_481944.jpg/330px-Site_preparation_for_new_warehouse._-_geograph.org.uk_-_481944.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Site_preparation_for_new_warehouse._-_geograph.org.uk_-_481944.jpg/440px-Site_preparation_for_new_warehouse._-_geograph.org.uk_-_481944.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Site_preparation_for_new_warehouse._-_geograph.org.uk_-_481944.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>ASOS <a href="/wiki/Distribution_center" title="Distribution center">distribution centre</a> (former <a href="/wiki/Prologis" title="Prologis">Prologis</a> before 2010) being built in 2006 at Little Houghton</div></div></div>
<p>North-east of Barnsley is Ardagh Glass at Monk Bretton. Slightly further north is Mr Kipling at Carlton; the site was <a href="/wiki/J._Lyons_and_Co." title="J. Lyons and Co.">Lyons Cakes</a> (making their <a href="/wiki/Battenberg_cake" title="Battenberg cake">Battenberg cakes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Viennese_Whirls" title="Viennese Whirls">Viennese Whirls</a> and <a href="/wiki/Swiss_roll" title="Swiss roll">Swiss rolls</a>) before April 1995, then RHM's Manor Bakeries until 2007, and makes their <i>exceedingly good</i> fruit pies; one million chocolate <a href="/wiki/Yule_log_(cake)" title="Yule log (cake)">yule logs</a> are made there and it is the largest <a href="/wiki/Mince_pie" title="Mince pie">mince pie</a> factory in the world. <a href="/wiki/Fulton%27s_Foods" title="Fulton&#39;s Foods">Jack Fulton</a> (Frozen Value Ltd) is next to the <a href="/wiki/Hallam_Line" title="Hallam Line">railway</a>, off the A637 at Darton. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wharncliffe_Publishing&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Wharncliffe Publishing (page does not exist)">Wharncliffe Publishing</a> are in Barnsley, and to the east on the <a href="/wiki/A628_road" title="A628 road">A628</a> in Oakwell, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Potters_(company)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Potters (company) (page does not exist)">Potters Europe</a> (former <a href="/w/index.php?title=Ballotini&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Ballotini (page does not exist)">Ballotini</a>) make <a href="/wiki/Glass_microsphere" title="Glass microsphere">glass microspheres</a> for <a href="/wiki/Raised_pavement_marker" title="Raised pavement marker">road reflectors</a>. <a href="/wiki/Galpharm_International" title="Galpharm International">Galpharm International</a> (bought by <a href="/wiki/Perrigo" title="Perrigo">Perrigo</a> in January 2008) and <a href="/wiki/JTEKT" title="JTEKT">Koyo Bearings</a> are at <a href="/wiki/Dodworth" title="Dodworth">Dodworth</a> near Barnsley. <a href="/wiki/CELSA_Group" title="CELSA Group">BRC</a> on the Claycliffe Ind Estate, off the A637 in the north of Barnsley, makes <a href="/wiki/Rebar" title="Rebar">rebar</a> (steel reinforcement). Naylor Industries, off the B6096 between Wombwell and <a href="/wiki/Darfield,_South_Yorkshire" title="Darfield, South Yorkshire">Darfield</a> make <a href="/wiki/Earthenware" title="Earthenware">earthenware</a> pipes for drainage. <a href="/wiki/Kostal" class="mw-redirect" title="Kostal">Kostal</a> UK make <a href="/wiki/Steering_column" title="Steering column">steering column</a> switches and <a href="/wiki/Electrical_connector" title="Electrical connector">electrical connectors</a> off the <a href="/wiki/A635_road" title="A635 road">A635</a> at Highgate in <a href="/wiki/Goldthorpe" title="Goldthorpe">Goldthorpe</a>. On the <a href="/wiki/A6195_road" title="A6195 road">A6195</a> <a href="/wiki/Grimethorpe" title="Grimethorpe">Grimethorpe</a> Bypass at <a href="/wiki/Little_Houghton,_South_Yorkshire" title="Little Houghton, South Yorkshire">Little Houghton</a> is the NDC of <a href="/wiki/ASOS.com" title="ASOS.com">ASOS.com</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Dearne_Valley" title="Dearne Valley">Dearne Valley</a>, near the former site of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Houghton_Main_Colliery&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Houghton Main Colliery (page does not exist)">Houghton Main Colliery</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lotus_Professional&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lotus Professional (page does not exist)">Lotus Professional</a> (owned since 2012 by <a href="/wiki/SCA_(company)" title="SCA (company)">SCA</a>) is off the <a href="/wiki/A6102_road" class="mw-redirect" title="A6102 road">A6102</a> north of <a href="/wiki/Oughtibridge" title="Oughtibridge">Oughtibridge</a>, north-west of Sheffield, in <a href="/wiki/Wortley,_South_Yorkshire" title="Wortley, South Yorkshire">Wortley</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/DFS_Furniture" title="DFS Furniture">DFS</a> is at <a href="/wiki/Adwick_le_Street" title="Adwick le Street">Adwick le Street</a> near the A1/<a href="/wiki/A638_road" title="A638 road">A638</a> junction. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Crompton_Lighting&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Crompton Lighting (page does not exist)">Crompton Lighting</a> have their main factory in <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wheatley,_South_Yorkshire&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Wheatley, South Yorkshire (page does not exist)">Wheatley Park</a> on the <a href="/wiki/A630_road" title="A630 road">A630</a> in north-east Doncaster. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Unipart_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Unipart Rail (page does not exist)">Unipart Rail</a> have a headquarters next to <a href="/wiki/Wabtec_Corporation" title="Wabtec Corporation">Wabtec Rail</a>, who make <a href="/wiki/Railway_air_brake" title="Railway air brake">railway air brakes</a>, off the <a href="/wiki/A6182_road" title="A6182 road">A6182</a> near <a href="/wiki/Potteric_Carr" title="Potteric Carr">Potteric Carr</a> at the J3 Business Park, near VolkerRail; nearby are two Amazon <a href="/wiki/Fulfillment_house" title="Fulfillment house">fulfilment centres</a>, with another at the <a href="/wiki/Doncaster_iPort" title="Doncaster iPort">Doncaster iPort</a> in Rossington. <a href="/wiki/Relate" title="Relate">Relate</a> (former Marriage Guidance Council) is based off the A6182 – and on same site <a href="/wiki/VolkerRail" title="VolkerRail">VolkerRail</a> Doncaster is next to <a href="/wiki/DB_Cargo_UK" title="DB Cargo UK">DB Cargo UK</a> (former EWS), <a href="/w/index.php?title=Schenck_Process&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Schenck Process (page does not exist)">Schenck Process</a> UK, and Thales have a data centre next door. <a href="/wiki/OASys_(company)" class="mw-redirect" title="OASys (company)">Webasto</a> have their UK headquarters next to Lakeside Village, Doncaster on the A6182, and make sunroofs and <a href="/wiki/HVAC" class="mw-redirect" title="HVAC">air-conditioning systems</a>. <a href="/wiki/McCormick_Tractors" title="McCormick Tractors">McCormick Tractors</a> had a tractor plant in Doncaster until 2007. <a href="/wiki/Bridon_Ropes" title="Bridon Ropes">Bridon International</a>, a world-leading manufacturer of wire ropes (part of <a href="/wiki/Melrose_Industries" title="Melrose Industries">Melrose Industries</a>), are based at Balby Carr, off St Catherines Interchange junction 3 of the M18, and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Montracon&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Montracon (page does not exist)">Montracon</a> (<a href="/wiki/Semi-trailer_truck" title="Semi-trailer truck">vehicle trailers</a>) are headquartered there, with a manufacturing site at <a href="/wiki/Market_Weighton" title="Market Weighton">Market Weighton</a>; nearby are <a href="/w/index.php?title=Darfen_Durafencing&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Darfen Durafencing (page does not exist)">Darfen Durafencing</a> have been trading for over 100 years, and are the market leader in permanent fencing. <a href="/wiki/Pegler_Yorkshire" title="Pegler Yorkshire">Pegler Yorkshire</a> (owned by <a href="/wiki/Aalberts_Industries" title="Aalberts Industries">Aalberts Industries</a>) are near the A630 in Balby Carr, further along from Bridon, with <a href="/w/index.php?title=MSI-Quality_Forgings&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="MSI-Quality Forgings (page does not exist)">MSI-Quality Forgings</a> opposite with <a href="/w/index.php?title=Global-MSI&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Global-MSI (page does not exist)">Global-MSI</a> who manufacture <a href="/wiki/Filling_station" title="Filling station">petrol station</a> <a href="/wiki/Forecourt" title="Forecourt">forecourts</a>. <a href="/wiki/Polypipe" title="Polypipe">Polypipe</a> (<a href="/wiki/Polyvinyl_chloride" title="Polyvinyl chloride">uPVC</a> pipes) is in <a href="/wiki/New_Edlington" title="New Edlington">Edlington</a>. CME Sanitary Systems in Warmsworth (a former division of Polypipe, now owned by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wirquin_(company)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Wirquin (company) (page does not exist)">Wirquin</a> of France) makes the UK's best selling plastic <a href="/wiki/Toilet_seat" title="Toilet seat">toilet seats</a> off the Warmsworth Interchange of the A1(M). <a href="/wiki/Fellowes_Brands" title="Fellowes Brands">Fellowes</a> UK (stationery) is based on West Moor Park, off West Moor Interchange junction 4 of the M18 (<a href="/wiki/A630_road" title="A630 road">A630</a>) in <a href="/wiki/Armthorpe" title="Armthorpe">Armthorpe</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wirquin_(company)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Wirquin (company) (page does not exist)">Wirquin</a> UK (plumbing) is off the B6376 in <a href="/wiki/Warmsworth" title="Warmsworth">Warmsworth</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yorkshire_and_the_Humber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_England" title="Sport in England">Sport in England</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Sheffield" title="Sport in Sheffield">Sport in Sheffield</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/English_Institute_of_Sport" title="English Institute of Sport">English Institute of Sport</a> is <a href="/wiki/English_Institute_of_Sport,_Sheffield" title="English Institute of Sport, Sheffield">situated</a> in north-east Sheffield, towards <a href="/wiki/Tinsley_Viaduct" title="Tinsley Viaduct">Tinsley Viaduct</a>; it is the home of many indoor national sports teams, and <a href="/wiki/Basketball_England" title="Basketball England">Basketball England</a>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Sports_Turf_Research_Institute" title="Sports Turf Research Institute">Sports Turf Research Institute</a>, off the B6459 at <a href="/wiki/Bingley_St_Ives" title="Bingley St Ives">Bingley St Ives</a> in <a href="/wiki/Harden,_West_Yorkshire" title="Harden, West Yorkshire">Harden</a>, west of Bingley, is the
world authority on natural and artificial sports turf.
</p><p>Sheffield is the home of UK climbing, being near the <a href="/wiki/Rock_climbing_in_the_Peak_District" title="Rock climbing in the Peak District">Peak District</a>, and most well-known climbs are at <a href="/wiki/Malham_Cove" title="Malham Cove">Malham Cove</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kilnsey" title="Kilnsey">Kilnsey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gordale_Scar" title="Gordale Scar">Gordale</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yorkshire_and_the_Humber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The region is home to numerous <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> and <a href="/wiki/Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League">Football League</a> clubs. Leeds United, Sheffield Wednesday, Sheffield United and Huddersfield Town are the most successful clubs in the region in terms of trophies won, each winning 9, 9, 5 and 4 major trophies respectively. Leeds United are the most successful club in terms of European appearances and success, they have also been the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_coefficients#Top_club_by_period" class="mw-redirect" title="UEFA coefficients">UEFA coefficient Top Club</a> on 3 occasions, more than any other English club.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sheffield_F.C." title="Sheffield F.C.">Sheffield F.C.</a>, founded in October 1857, is the world's oldest football club still in existence; they play in the <a href="/wiki/Bostik" title="Bostik">Evo-Stik</a> <a href="/wiki/Northern_Premier_League" title="Northern Premier League">Northern Premier League</a>. The world's first inter-club match took place on 26 December 1860 between this club and <a href="/wiki/Hallam_F.C." title="Hallam F.C.">Hallam F.C.</a>. <a href="/wiki/Herbert_Chapman" title="Herbert Chapman">Herbert Chapman</a> introduced numbered shirts. The <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Rules" title="Sheffield Rules">Sheffield Rules</a> introduced <a href="/wiki/Direct_free_kick" title="Direct free kick">free-kicks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corner_kick" title="Corner kick">corners</a> and <a href="/wiki/Throw-in" title="Throw-in">throw-ins</a>.
</p><p>On 9 May 1867 <a href="/wiki/Football_in_Argentina" title="Football in Argentina">Thomas Hogg and James Hogg</a> from <a href="/wiki/Skelton,_York" title="Skelton, York">Skelton</a> introduced football to South America in Argentina, founding <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires_Football_Club" title="Buenos Aires Football Club">Buenos Aires Football Club</a>.
</p><p>Here is a list of the Football League clubs in the region ranked in their league position at the end of the <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_in_English_football" title="2018–19 in English football">2018–19 season</a>.
</p>
<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Huddersfield_Town_A.F.C." title="Huddersfield Town A.F.C.">Huddersfield Town</a>, 20th in the <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> (relegated)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sheffield_United_F.C." title="Sheffield United F.C.">Sheffield United</a>, 2nd in the <a href="/wiki/EFL_Championship" title="EFL Championship">Championship</a>. (promoted)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Leeds_United_F.C." title="Leeds United F.C.">Leeds United</a>, 3rd in the Championship.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sheffield_Wednesday_F.C." title="Sheffield Wednesday F.C.">Sheffield Wednesday</a>, 12th in the Championship.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hull_City_A.F.C." title="Hull City A.F.C.">Hull City</a>, 13th in the Championship.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rotherham_United_F.C." title="Rotherham United F.C.">Rotherham United</a>, 22nd in the Championship. (relegated)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Barnsley_F.C." title="Barnsley F.C.">Barnsley</a>, 2nd in <a href="/wiki/EFL_League_One" title="EFL League One">League One</a>. (promoted)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Doncaster_Rovers_F.C." title="Doncaster Rovers F.C.">Doncaster Rovers</a>, 6th in League One.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Scunthorpe_United_F.C." title="Scunthorpe United F.C.">Scunthorpe United</a>, 23rd in League One. (relegated)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bradford_City_A.F.C." title="Bradford City A.F.C.">Bradford City</a>, 24th in League One. (relegated)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Grimsby_Town_F.C." title="Grimsby Town F.C.">Grimsby Town</a>, 17th in <a href="/wiki/EFL_League_Two" title="EFL League Two">League Two</a>.</li></ol>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rugby_League">Rugby League</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yorkshire_and_the_Humber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Rugby League">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_rugby_league" title="History of rugby league">History of rugby league</a></div>
<p>The area, similar to north Cheshire and parts of Greater Manchester (along the <a href="/wiki/M62_motorway" title="M62 motorway">M62</a>), is synonymous with <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a>. <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanya_Arnold&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tanya Arnold (page does not exist)">Tanya Arnold</a>, presents the BBC rugby league programme <i><a href="/wiki/Super_League_Show" title="Super League Show">Super League Show</a></i>, broadcast nationwide from Leeds. On 22 August 1895 at the George Hotel in Huddersfield, twenty-two northern rugby clubs formed the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Rugby_Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Rugby Football League">Rugby Football League</a>; the RFL is now based in the north-east of Leeds.
</p><p>Local teams are:

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Horse_racing">Horse racing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yorkshire_and_the_Humber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Horse racing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/St_Leger_Stakes" title="St Leger Stakes">St Leger Stakes</a>, at <a href="/wiki/Doncaster_Racecourse" title="Doncaster Racecourse">Doncaster Racecourse</a>, is the world's oldest <a href="/wiki/British_Classic_Races" title="British Classic Races">classic</a> horse race, first run in 1776, founded by Major-General <a href="/wiki/Anthony_St_Leger_(British_Army_officer)" title="Anthony St Leger (British Army officer)">Anthony St. Leger</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Doncaster_Cup" title="Doncaster Cup">Doncaster Cup</a>, first run in 1766, is the world's oldest continuing regulated horse race.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cricket">Cricket</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yorkshire_and_the_Humber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Cricket">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Jim_Laker" title="Jim Laker">Jim Laker</a>, of Saltaire, took 46 wickets in a <a href="/wiki/Test_cricket" title="Test cricket">5-test series</a>, a record.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yorkshire_and_the_Humber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>There are 15 <a href="/wiki/Local_education_authority" title="Local education authority">local education authorities</a> in the Yorkshire and Humber region.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The schools in each authority are listed in the following –
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:South_Hunsley_School_Melton_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/South_Hunsley_School_Melton_1.jpg/220px-South_Hunsley_School_Melton_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/South_Hunsley_School_Melton_1.jpg/330px-South_Hunsley_School_Melton_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/South_Hunsley_School_Melton_1.jpg/440px-South_Hunsley_School_Melton_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:South_Hunsley_School_Melton_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/South_Hunsley_School" title="South Hunsley School">South Hunsley School</a></div></div></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Secondary_education">Secondary education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yorkshire_and_the_Humber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Secondary education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Schools are mostly comprehensive, with some <a href="/wiki/Grammar_schools_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammar schools in the United Kingdom">grammar schools</a> in North Yorkshire, Calderdale and Kirklees.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are around 235,000 at the region's secondary schools, the 4th lowest for English regions. The region has the highest overall <a href="/wiki/Truancy" title="Truancy">truancy</a> rate in England for both urban and rural areas. Inside the region for districts, Leeds has the highest rate with 6.9% persistent truants at secondary school, then Hull is second with 6.3%. Calderdale has the lowest truancy rate for unitary authorities, almost half that of Leeds, followed by <a href="/wiki/North_Lincolnshire" title="North Lincolnshire">North Lincolnshire</a>. For districts <a href="/wiki/Craven" title="Craven">Craven</a> has the lowest rate.
</p><p>The schools in Hull have often performed among the worst (on average) in England at <a href="/wiki/General_Certificate_of_Secondary_Education" title="General Certificate of Secondary Education">GCSE</a><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> after <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Borough_of_Knowsley" title="Metropolitan Borough of Knowsley">Knowsley</a> in Merseyside. To Hull's credit, three schools in its LEA get above-average GCSE results whereas Knowsley usually has none (it managed two in 2010). Also at GCSE, schools in Barnsley and Bradford have low-achieving results with Barnsley the worst of these, and the lowest in the region in 2010. All three of these areas coincidentally have an above-average <a href="/wiki/Teenage_pregnancy_and_sexual_health_in_the_United_Kingdom" class="mw-redirect" title="Teenage pregnancy and sexual health in the United Kingdom">teenage pregnancy</a> problem. In past years, Doncaster would be included in this group, but has managed to perform much better. For the metropolitan areas, Calderdale and Wakefield consistently perform the best, with both above the England average. Rotherham usually has the best results in South Yorkshire, but in 2010 it was Doncaster. York and North Yorkshire consistently perform the best at GCSE in the region, and with the East Riding of Yorkshire have results above the UK average.
</p><p>Schoolchildren in Kingston upon Hull are most likely not to pass any GCSEs – over 6% with Bradford having a similar proportion, closely followed by Sheffield and North East Lincolnshire. The East Riding of Yorkshire and North Lincolnshire have the fewest not passing any GCSEs, followed by York.
</p><p>For OFSTED inspections across England, the region has the highest proportion of schools (2.7%) with bad behaviour and the lowest proportion (16.3%) of schools with good behaviour. <a href="/wiki/South_West_England" title="South West England">South West England</a> has the best behaving schoolchildren. Inside the region, Hull has the highest proportion (16.7%) of schools with bad behaviour – the worst in England (Wandsworth and Bristol come joint second) – and York schools have the highest proportion (30%) of schools with outstanding behaviour.
</p><p>At <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Level_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="Advanced Level (UK)">A-level</a> North Lincolnshire, Kirklees, Hull, York and North Yorkshire perform quite well with Kirklees consistently being the best by a large margin and one of the highest in England, all having results above the England average. Wakefield and Calderdale were also close to the England average. The excellent Kirklees result is due to Greenhead College in Huddersfield, and North Lincolnshire's results are due to the <a href="/wiki/John_Leggott_College" title="John Leggott College">John Leggott College</a>, also a <a href="/wiki/Sixth_form_college" title="Sixth form college">sixth form college</a>. The districts of South Yorkshire perform the least in the area at A-level with Rotherham having the best results in this area, slightly below-average, and the other three districts achieve similar results, much lower than those in the former districts of Humberside. Leeds and Bradford now get the lowest results in West Yorkshire.
</p><p>For both A-level and GCSE, Barnsley and Bradford are very low performing, with Barnsley usually getting the lowest A-level results in the region, but in 2010 North East Lincolnshire came bottom with unusually low results. Hull and northern Lincolnshire have a wide socio-economic diversity – many under-achieving pupils at 16 but with high performers at A-level. Hull, although much worse at GCSE, outperforms the East Riding of Yorkshire at A-level.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>School children in North Yorkshire (with York and Kirklees) are the most likely to go to university – they also get the best A level results, and those in the East Riding of Yorkshire are likely to go to university, but get lower overall A level results.
</p>
<h3><span id="Top_twenty_state_schools_in_Yorkshire_and_the_Humber_.282015_A-level_results.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Top_twenty_state_schools_in_Yorkshire_and_the_Humber_(2015_A-level_results)">Top twenty state schools in Yorkshire and the Humber (2015 A-level results)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yorkshire_and_the_Humber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Top twenty state schools in Yorkshire and the Humber (2015 A-level results)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Colleges">Colleges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yorkshire_and_the_Humber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Colleges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are twenty seven FE colleges. The main four colleges are Bradford College, East Riding College, Doncaster College, Grimsby Institute, and Hull College.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Leeds_(4th_May_2010)_061.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/University_of_Leeds_%284th_May_2010%29_061.jpg/220px-University_of_Leeds_%284th_May_2010%29_061.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/University_of_Leeds_%284th_May_2010%29_061.jpg/330px-University_of_Leeds_%284th_May_2010%29_061.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/University_of_Leeds_%284th_May_2010%29_061.jpg/440px-University_of_Leeds_%284th_May_2010%29_061.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Leeds_(4th_May_2010)_061.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Leeds" title="University of Leeds">University of Leeds</a> – looking towards the Roger Stevens Building</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Universities">Universities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Yorkshire_and_the_Humber&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Universities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_universities_in_Yorkshire_and_the_Humber" title="List of universities in Yorkshire and the Humber">List of universities in Yorkshire and the Humber</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:142px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Arts_tower.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Arts_tower.jpg/140px-Arts_tower.jpg" decoding="async" width="140" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Arts_tower.jpg/210px-Arts_tower.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Arts_tower.jpg/280px-Arts_tower.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2193" data-file-height="3442" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Arts_tower.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The University of Sheffield's <a href="/wiki/Arts_Tower" title="Arts Tower">Arts Tower</a> (1966) is the tallest university building in the UK at 78 metres (255&#160;ft), although <a href="/wiki/Imperial_College_London" title="Imperial College London">Imperial College</a>'s decorative <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Tower_(London)" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen&#39;s Tower (London)">Queen's Tower</a> is 87 metres (287&#160;ft) and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Birmingham" title="University of Birmingham">University of Birmingham</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Chamberlain_Memorial_Clock_Tower" title="Joseph Chamberlain Memorial Clock Tower">clock tower</a> is around 100 metres (330&#160;ft)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></div></div></div>
<p>There are ten universities and three higher education colleges in Yorkshire and the Humber, along with (in 2007) 27 Further Education colleges teaching some Higher Education courses.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Citric_acid_cycle" title="Citric acid cycle">Krebs Cycle</a> was discovered at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Sheffield" title="University of Sheffield">University of Sheffield</a> in 1937. <a href="/wiki/Liquid_crystal_display" class="mw-redirect" title="Liquid crystal display">Liquid crystal displays</a> were developed by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Hull" title="University of Hull">University of Hull</a> in 1972, in conjunction with the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Radar_Establishment" title="Royal Radar Establishment">Royal Radar Establishment</a> in <a href="/wiki/Worcestershire" title="Worcestershire">Worcestershire</a>. Low fat spreads were developed at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Leeds" title="University of Leeds">University of Leeds</a> (in conjunction with <a href="/wiki/Unilever" title="Unilever">Unilever</a>) in the 1980s, and in the 1930s <a href="/wiki/William_Astbury" title="William Astbury">William Astbury</a>'s <a href="/wiki/X-ray_scattering_techniques" title="X-ray scattering techniques">x-ray diffraction</a> experiments at the university started the road to the discovery of the double helix structure.
</p><p>Sheffield Hallam University is the largest in the region with 37,000 students, but does not have the most funding. The University of Leeds is not too far behind. The University of York, a large campus similar to a <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_university" title="Collegiate university">collegiate university</a>, gets much less funding than Leeds and Sheffield, but has quite a high research grant for its size, about half that of Leeds or Sheffield. The other universities do not have large research grants. Leeds and Sheffield have around twice as much total income than any other university. York and Bradford are the two smallest universities.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>For first degree students at universities in the region, 27% are native to the region, 16% are from <a href="/wiki/North_West_England" title="North West England">North West England</a> and 11% from the <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands" title="East Midlands">East Midlands</a>; 48% are from Northern England and around 25% from Southern England.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Access to the M62 determines the regions from which the region's universities' students originate from – the nearer they are to the motorway the easier it is to study in the Yorkshire and Humberside region.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (March 2010)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> For first degree students native to the region, 43% stay in the region, 16% go to the North West, 11% to the North East and 11% to the <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands" title="East Midlands">East Midlands</a>; just under 10% go to <a href="/wiki/Southern_England" title="Southern England">Southern England</a>, with 70% staying in <a href="/wiki/Northern_England" title="Northern England">Northern England</a>.
</p><p>Once graduated, 53% of the region's universities' graduates (native and non-native) stay to find work in the region, with around 10% moving to the North West (Manchester); 70% stay in Northern England, with 20% going to Southern England.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
